\\tGenerateConfigPath string\\n109: }\\n110: \\n111: // See GraphBuilder\\n112: func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\\n113: Makes its decisions primarily based on the given configuration, which\n25: //     represents the desired state.\n26: //\n27: //   - Ignores certain lifecycle concerns like create_before_destroy, because\n28: //     those are only important once we already know what action we're planning\n29: //     to take against a particular resource instance.\n30: type PlanGraphBuilder struct {\n31: \t// Config is the configuration tree to build a plan from.\n32: \tConfig *configs.Config\n33: \n34: \t// State is the current state\n35: \tState *states.State\n36: \n37: \t// RootVariableValues are the raw input values for root input variables\n38: \t// given by the caller, which we'll resolve into final values as part\n39: \t// of the plan walk.\n40: \tRootVariableValues InputValues\n41: \n42: \t// ExternalProviderConfigs are pre-initialized root module provider\n43: \t// configurations that the graph builder should assume will be available\n44: \t// immediately during the subsequent plan walk, without any explicit\n45: \t// initialization step.\n46: \tExternalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n47: \n48: \t// Plugins is a library of plug-in components (providers and\n49: \t// provisioners) available for use.\n50: \tPlugins *contextPlugins\n51: \n52: \t// Targets are resources to target\n53: \tTargets []addrs.Targetable\n54: \n55: \t// ForceReplace are resource instances where if we would normally have\n56: \t// generated a NoOp or Update action then we'll force generating a replace\n57: \t// action instead. Create and Delete actions are not affected.\n58: \tForceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n59: \n60: \t// skipRefresh indicates that we should skip refreshing managed resources\n61: \tskipRefresh bool\n62: \n63: \t// preDestroyRefresh indicates that we are executing the refresh which\n64: \t// happens immediately before a destroy plan, which happens to use the\n65: \t// normal planing mode so skipPlanChanges cannot be set.\n66: \tpreDestroyRefresh bool\n67: \n68: \t// skipPlanChanges indicates that we should skip the step of comparing\n69: \t// prior state with configuration and generating planned changes to\n70: \t// resource instances. (This is for the \"refresh only\" planning mode,\n71: \t// where we _only_ do the refresh step.)\n72: \tskipPlanChanges bool\n73: \n74: \tConcreteProvider                ConcreteProviderNodeFunc\n75: \tConcreteResource                ConcreteResourceNodeFunc\n76: \tConcreteResourceInstance        ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc\n77: \tConcreteResourceOrphan          ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc\n78: \tConcreteResourceInstanceDeposed ConcreteResourceInstanceDeposedNodeFunc\n79: \tConcreteModule                  ConcreteModuleNodeFunc\n80: \n81: \t// Plan Operation this graph will be used for.\n82: \tOperation walkOperation\n83: \n84: \t// ExternalReferences allows the external caller to pass in references to\n85: \t// nodes that should not be pruned even if they are not referenced within\n86: \t// the actual graph.\n87: \tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\n88: \n89: \t// Overrides provides the set of overrides supplied by the testing\n90: \t// framework.\n91: \tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\n92: \n93: \t// ImportTargets are the list of resources to import.\n94: \tImportTargets []*ImportTarget\n95: \n96: \t// forgetResources lists the resources that are to be forgotten, i.e. removed\n97: \t// from state without destroying.\n98: \tforgetResources []addrs.ConfigResource\n99: \n100: \t// forgetModules lists the modules that are to be forgotten, i.e. removed\n101: \t// from state without destroying.\n102: \tforgetModules []addrs.Module\n103: \n104: \t// GenerateConfig tells Terraform where to write and generated config for\n105: \t// any import targets that do not already have configuration.\n106: \t//\n107: \t// If empty, then config will not be generated.\n108: \tGenerateConfigPath string\n109: }\n110: \n111: // See GraphBuilder\n112: func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n113: \tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] building graph for %s\", b.Operation)\n114: \treturn (&BasicGraphBuilder{\n115: \t\tSteps: b.Steps(),\n116: \t\tName:  \"PlanGraphBuilder\",\n117: \t}).Build(path)\n118: }\n119: \n120: // See GraphBuilder\n121: func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Steps() []GraphTransformer {\n122: \tswitch b.Operation {\n123: \tcase walkPlan:\n124: \t\tb.initPlan()\n125: \tcase walkPlanDestroy:\n126: \t\tb.initDestroy()\n127: \tcase walkValidate:\n128: (During plan this will\n195: \t\t// intentionally skip creating nodes for _current_ objects, since\n196: \t\t// ConfigTransformer created nodes that will do that during\n197: \t\t// DynamicExpand.)\n198: \t\t&StateTransformer{\n199: \t\t\tConcreteCurrent: b.ConcreteResourceInstance,\n200: \t\t\tConcreteDeposed: b.ConcreteResourceInstanceDeposed,\n201: \t\t\tState:           b.State,\n202: \t\t},\n203: \n204: \t\t// Attach the state\n205: \t\t&AttachStateTransformer{State: b.State},\n206: \n207: \t\t// Create orphan output nodes\n208: \t\t&OrphanOutputTransformer{\n209: \t\t\tConfig:   b.Config,\n210: \t\t\tState:    b.State,\n211: \t\t\tPlanning: true,\n212: \t\t},\n213: \n214: \t\t// Attach the configuration to any resources\n215: \t\t&AttachResourceConfigTransformer{Config: b.Config},\n216: \n217: \t\t// add providers\n218: \t\ttransformProviders(b.ConcreteProvider, b.Config, b.ExternalProviderConfigs),\n219: \n220: \t\t// Remove modules no longer present in the config\n221: \t\t&RemovedModuleTransformer{Config: b.Config, State: b.State},\n222: \n223: \t\t// Must attach schemas before ReferenceTransformer so that we can\n224: \t\t// analyze the configuration to find references.\n225: \t\t&AttachSchemaTransformer{Plugins: b.Plugins, Config: b.Config},\n226: \n227: \t\t// Create expansion nodes for all of the module calls. This must\n228: \t\t// come after all other transformers that create nodes representing\n229: \t\t// objects that can belong to modules.\n230: \t\t&ModuleExpansionTransformer{Concrete: b.ConcreteModule, Config: b.Config},\n231: \n232: \t\t// Plug in any external references.\n233: \t\t&ExternalReferenceTransformer{\n234: \t\t\tExternalReferences: b.ExternalReferences,\n235: \t\t},\n236: \n237: \t\t&ReferenceTransformer{},\n238: \n239: \t\t&AttachDependenciesTransformer{},\n240: \n241: \t\t// Make sure data sources are aware of any depends_on from the\n242: \t\t// We intentionally do this\\n453: \\t\\t\\t// _after_ writing the state/diff because we want to check against\\n454: \\t\\t\\t// the result of the operation, and to fail on future operations\\n455: \\t\\t\\t// until the user makes the condition succeed.\\n456: \\t\\t\\t// (Note that some preconditions will end up being skipped during\\n457: \\t\\t\\t// planning, because their conditions depend on values not yet known.)\\n458: \\t\\t\\tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\\n459: \\t\\t\\t\\taddrs.ResourcePostcondition,\\n460: \\t\\t\\t\\tn.Config.Postconditions,\\n461: \\t\\t\\t\\tctx, n.ResourceInstanceAddr(), repeatData,\\n462: \\t\\t\\t\\tcheckRuleSeverity,\\n463: \\t\\t\\t)\\n464: \\t\\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\\n465: \\t\\t} else {\\n466: \\t\\t\\t// The deferrals tracker says that we must defer changes for\\n467: \\t\\t\\t// this resource instance, presumably due to a dependency on an\\n468: \\t\\t\\t// upstream object that was already deferred. Therefore we just\\n469: \\t\\t\\t// report our own deferral (capturing a placeholder value in the\\n470: \\t\\t\\t// deferral tracker) and don't add anything to the plan or\\n471: \\t\\t\\t// working state.\\n472: \\t\\t\\t// In this case, the expression evaluator should use the placeholder\\n473: \\t\\t\\t// value registered here as the value of this resource instance,\\n474: \\t\\t\\t// instead of using the plan.\\n475: \\t\\t\\tdeferrals.ReportResourceInstanceDeferred(n.Addr, providers.DeferredReasonDeferredPrereq, change)\\n476: \\t\\t}\\n477: \\t} else {\\n478: \\t\\t// In refresh-only mode we need to evaluate the for-each expression in\\n479: \\t\\t// order to supply the value to the pre- and post-condition check\\n480: \\t\\t// blocks. Since this is a NoOp we know\\n440: \\t\\t\\t// that the stored dependencies will have no effect during apply, and we can\\n441: \\t\\t\\t// write them out now.\\n442: \\t\\t\\tif change.Action == plans.NoOp && !depsEqual(instanceRefreshState.Dependencies, n.Dependencies) {\\n443: \\t\\t\\t\\t// the refresh state will be the final state for this resource, so\\n444: \\t\\t\\t\\t// finalize the dependencies here if they need to be updated.\\n445: \\t\\t\\t\\tinstanceRefreshState.Dependencies = n.Dependencies\\n446: \\t\\t\\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instanceRefreshState, refreshState))\\n447: \\t\\t\\t\\tif diags.HasErrors() {\\n448: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\treturn diags\\n449: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n450: \\t\\t\\t}\\n451: \\n452: \\t\\t\\t// Post-conditions might block completion. We intentionally do this\\n453: \\t\\t\\t// _after_ writing the state/diff because we want to check against\\n454: \\t\\t\\t// the result of the operation, and to fail on future operations\\n455: \\t\\t\\t// until the user makes the condition succeed.\\n456: \\t\\t\\t// (Note that some preconditions will end up being skipped during\\n457: \\t\\t\\t// planning, because their conditions depend on values not yet known.)\\n458: \\t\\t\\tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\\n459: \\t\\t\\t\\taddrs.ResourcePostcondition,\\n460: \\t\\t\\t\\tn.Config.Postconditions,\\n461: \\t\\t\\t\\tctx, n.ResourceInstanceAddr(), repeatData,\\n462: \\t\\t\\t\\tcheckRuleSeverity,\\n463: \\t\\t\\t)\\n464: \\t\\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\\n465: \\t\\t} else {\\n466: \\t\\t\\t// The deferrals tracker says that we must defer changes for\\n467: \\t\\t\\t// this resource instance, presumably due to a dependency on an\\n468: \\t\\t\\t// upstream object that was already deferred. Therefore we just\\n469: \\t\\t\\t// report our own deferral (capturing a placeholder value in the\\n470: \\t\\t\\t// deferral tracker) and don't add anything to the plan or\\n471: \\t\\t\\t// working state.\\n472: \\t\\t\\t// In this case, the expression evaluator should use the placeholder\\n473: \\t\\t\\t// value registered here as the value of this resource instance,\\n474: \\t\\t\\t// instead of using the plan.\\n475: \\t\\t\\tdeferrals.ReportResourceInstanceDeferred(n.Addr, providers.DeferredReasonDeferredPrereq, change)\\n476: \\t\\t}\\n477: \\t} else {\\n478: \\t\\t// In refresh-only mode we need to evaluate the for-each expression in\\n479: \\t\\t// order to supply the value to the pre- and post-condition check\\n480: \\t\\t// blocks. deferred either during the import,\n400: \t\t\t// refresh or planning stage. We'll report the deferral and\n401: \t\t\t// store what we could produce in the deferral tracker.\n402: \t\t\tdeferrals.ReportResourceInstanceDeferred(addr, deferred.Reason, change)\n403: \t\t} else if !deferrals.ShouldDeferResourceInstanceChanges(n.Addr, n.Dependencies) {\n404: \t\t\t// We intentionally write the change before the subsequent checks, because\n405: \t\t\t// all of the checks below this point are for problems caused by the\n406: \t\t\t// context surrounding the change, rather than the change itself, and\n407: \t\t\t// so it's helpful to still include the valid-in-isolation change as\n408: \t\t\t// part of the plan as additional context in our error output.\n409: \t\t\t//\n410: \t\t\t// FIXME: it is currently important that we write resource changes to\n411: \t\t\t// the plan (n.writeChange) before we write the corresponding state\n412: \t\t\t// (n.writeResourceInstanceState).\n413: \t\t\t//\n414: \t\t\t// This is because the planned resource state will normally have the\n415: \t\t\t// status of states.ObjectPlanned, which causes later logic to refer to\n416: \t\t\t// the contents of the plan to retrieve the resource data. Because\n417: \t\t\t// there is no shared lock between these two data structures, reversing\n418: \t\t\t// the order of these writes will cause a brief window of inconsistency\n419: \t\t\t// which can lead to a failed safety check.\n420: \t\t\t//\n421: \t\t\t// Future work should adjust these APIs such that it is impossible to\n422: \t\t\t// update these two data structures incorrectly through any objects\n423: \t\t\t// reachable via the terraform.EvalContext API.\n424: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(n.writeChange(ctx, change, \"\"))\n425: \t\t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n426: \t\t\t\treturn diags\n427: \t\t\t}\n428: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instancePlanState, workingState))\n429: \t\t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n430: \t\t\t\treturn diags\n431: \t\t\t}\n432: \n433: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(n.checkPreventDestroy(change))\n434: \t\t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n435: \t\t\t\treturn diags\n436: \t\t\t}\n437: \n438: \t\t\t// If this plan resulted in a NoOp, then apply won't have a chance to make\n439: \t\t\t// any changes to the stored dependencies. Since this is a NoOp we know\n440: \t\t\t// that the stored dependencies will have no effect during apply, and we can\n441: \t\t\t// write them out now.\n442: \t\t\tif change.Action == plans.NoOp && !depsEqual(instanceRefreshState.Dependencies, n.Dependencies) {\n443: \t\t\t\t// the refresh state will be the final state for this resource, so\n444: \t\t\t\t// finalize the dependencies here if they need to be updated.\n445: \t\t\t\tinstanceRefreshState.Dependencies = n.Dependencies\n446: \t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instanceRefreshState, refreshState))\n447: \t\t\t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n448: \t\t\t\t\treturn diags\n449: \t\t\t\t}\n450: \t\t\t}\n451: \n452: \t\t\t// Post-conditions might block completion. We intentionally do this\n453: \t\t\t// _after_ writing the state/diff because we want to check against\n454: \t\t\t// the result of the operation, and to fail on future operations\n455: \t\t\t// until the user makes the condition succeed.\n456: \t\t\t// (Note that some preconditions will end up being skipped during\n457: \t\t\t// planning, because their conditions depend on values not yet known.)\n458: \t\t\tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n459: \t\t\t\taddrs.ResourcePostcondition,\n460: \t\t\t\tn.Config.Postconditions,\n461: \t\t\t\tctx, n.ResourceInstanceAddr(), repeatData,\n462: \t\t\t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n463: \t\t\t)\n464: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n465: \t\t} else {\n466: \t\t\t// The deferrals tracker says that we must defer changes for\n467: \t\t\t// this resource instance, presumably due to a dependency on an\n468: \t\t\t// upstream object that was already deferred. Therefore we just\n469: \t\t\t// report our own deferral (capturing a placeholder value in the\n470: \t\t\t// deferral tracker) and don't add anything to the plan or\n471: \t\t\t// working state.\n472: \t\t\t// In this case, the expression evaluator should use the placeholder\n473: \t\t\t// value registered here as the value of this resource instance,\n474: \t\t\t// instead of using the plan.\n475: \t\t\tdeferrals.ReportResourceInstanceDeferred(n.Addr, providers.DeferredReasonDeferredPrereq, change)\n476: \t\t}\n477: \t} else {\n478: \t\t// In refresh-only mode we need to evaluate the for-each expression in\n479: \t\t// order to supply the value to the pre- and post-condition check\n480: \t\t// blocks. This has the unfortunate edge case of a refresh-only plan\n481: \t\t// executing with a for-each map which has the same keys but different\n482: \t\t// values, which could result in a post-condition check relying on that\n483: \t\t// value being inaccurate. Unless we decide to store the value of the\n484: \t\t// for-each expression in state, this is unavoidable.\n485: \t\tforEach, _, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(n.Config.ForEach, ctx, false)\n486: \t\trepeatData := EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n487: \n488: \t\tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n489: \t\t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n490: \t\t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n491: \t\t\tctx, addr, repeatData,\n492: \t\t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n493: \t\t)\n494: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n495: \n496: \t\t// Even if we don't plan changes, we do still need to at least update\n497: \t\t// the working state to reflect the refresh result. If not, then e.g.\n498: \t\t// any output values refering to this will not react to the drift.\n499: \t\t// (Even if we didn't actually refresh above, this will still save\n500: \t\t// the result of any schema upgrading we did in readResourceInstanceState.)\n501: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instanceRefreshState, workingState))\n502: \t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n503: \t\t\treturn diags\n504: \t\t}\n505: \n506: \t\t// Here we also evaluate post-conditions after updating the working\n507: \t\t// state, because we want to check against the result of the refresh.\n508: \t\t// Unlike in normal planning mode, these checks are still evaluated\n509: \t\t// even if pre-conditions generated diagnostics, because we have no\n510: \t\t// planned changes to block.\n511: \t\tcheckDiags = evalCheckRules(\n512: \t\t\taddrs.ResourcePostcondition,\n513: \t\t\tn.Config.Postconditions,\n514: \t\t\tctx, addr, repeatData,\n515: \t\t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n516: \t\t)\n517: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n518: \n519: \t\t// In this case we skipped planning changes and therefore need to report the deferral\n520: \t\t// here, if there was one.\n521: \t\tif refreshDeferred != nil {\n522: \t\t\tctx.Deferrals().ReportResourceInstanceDeferred(addr, deferred.Reason, &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n523: \t\t\t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n524: \t\t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.Addr,\n525: \t\t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n526: \t\t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n527: \t\t\t\t\tAction: plans.Read,\n528: \t\t\t\t\tBefore: priorInstanceRefreshState.Value,\n529: \t\t\t\t\tAfter:  instanceRefreshState.Value,\n530: \t\t\t\t},\n531: \t\t\t})\n532: \t\t}\n533: \t}\n534: \n535: \treturn diags\n536: }\n537: \n538: // replaceTriggered checks if this instance needs to be replace due to a change\n539: // in a replace_triggered_by reference. If replacement is required, the\n540: // instance address is added to forceReplace\n541: func (n *NodePlannableResourceInstance) replaceTriggered(ctx EvalContext, repData instances.RepetitionData) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n542: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n543: \tif n.Config == nil {\n544: \t\treturn diags\n545: \t}\n546: \n547: \tfor _, expr := range n.Config.TriggersReplacement {\n548: \t\tref, replace, evalDiags := ctx.EvaluateReplaceTriggeredBy(expr, repData)\n549: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(evalDiags)\n550: \t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n551: \t\t\tcontinue\n552: \t\t}\n553: \n554: \t\tif replace {\n555: \t\t\t// FIXME: forceReplace accomplishes the same goal, however we may\n556: \t\t\t// want to communicate more information about which resource\n557: \t\t\t// triggered the replacement in the plan.\n558: \t\t\t// Rather than further complicating the plan method with more\n559: \t\t\t// options, we can refactor both of these features later.\n560: \t\t\tn.forceReplace = append(n.forceReplace, n.Addr)\n561: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] ReplaceTriggeredBy forcing replacement of %s due to change in %s\", n.Addr, ref.DisplayString())\n562: \n563: \t\t\tn.replaceTriggeredBy = append(n.replaceTriggeredBy, ref)\n564: \t\t\tbreak\n565: \t\t}\n566: \t}\n567: \n568: \treturn diags\n569: }\n570: \n571: func (n *NodePlannableResourceInstance) importState(ctx EvalContext, addr Transformer Sequence\n**File**: `internal/terraform/graph_builder_plan.go:121`\n\nThe `PlanGraphBuilder.Steps()` method returns a sequence of `GraphTransformer` stages that build the dependency graph:\n\n#### Stage 1: Node Creation (lines 135-202)\n1. **ConfigTransformer** (line 137): Creates resource nodes from configuration\n   - Adds all managed and data resources from the config tree\n   - Marks whether this is a destroy operation\n   - Handles import targets and configuration generation\n\n2. **Variable and Output Transformers** (lines 149-176):\n   - Attaches provider schemas to nodes\n   - Enables reference analysis based on schema information\n\n#### Stage 3: Module and Reference Processing (lines 227-239)\n7. **ModuleExpansionTransformer** (line 230): Creates expansion nodes for module calls\n\n8. **ExternalReferenceTransformer** (line 233): Preserves externally referenced nodes\n\n9. **ReferenceTransformer** (line 237): **Creates dependency edges from references**\n   - Analyzes all node references to find what each node depends on\n   - Connects edges from referencing nodes to their dependencies\n   - Implementation covered in detail below\n\n10. **AttachDependenciesTransformer** (line 239): Attaches explicit dependencies\n    - Processes depends_on arguments in resource configuration\n\n11. **attachDataResourceDependsOnTransformer** (line 243): Handles data resource depends_on\n\n#### Stage 4: Lifecycle and Cleanup (lines 245-274)\n12. **DestroyEdgeTransformer** (line 247): Creates edges for destroy operations\n13. **pruneUnusedNodesTransformer** (line 251): Removes unused nodes\n14. **TargetsTransformer** (line 256): Filters graph to only targeted resources (with dependencies)\n15. **ForcedCBDTransformer** (line 260): Forces create-before-destroy where needed\n16. **ephemeralResourceCloseTransformer** (line 263): Closes ephemeral resources\n17. **CloseProviderTransformer** (line 266): **Adds edges to properly close providers**\n18. **CloseRootModuleTransformer** (line 269): Closes the root module\n19. **TransitiveReductionTransformer** (line 273): Removes redundant edges\n\n### ReferenceTransformer - Dependency Edge Creation\n**File**: `internal/terraform/transform_reference.go:108-156`\n\nThe `ReferenceTransformer` analyzes configuration references to build dependency edges:\n\n```go\nfunc (t *ReferenceTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error\n```\n\n**Key Interface Requirements**:\n- **GraphNodeReferenceable**: Implemented by nodes that can be referenced (resources, modules, variables, outputs)\n  - `ReferenceableAddrs()`: Returns addresses through which this node can be referenced\n\n- **GraphNodeReferencer**: Implemented by nodes that reference other terraform objects\n  - `References()`: Returns a list of `addrs.Reference` objects being referenced\n\n**Algorithm** (lines 112-156):\n1. Builds a `ReferenceMap` from all graph vertices (line 115)\n2. For each vertex that implements `GraphNodeReferencer`:\n   - Calls `m.References(v)` to find parent dependencies (line 125)\n   - For each parent that is NOT a destroy node (to avoid cycles):\n     - Creates a `dag.BasicEdge` from the referencing node to the parent (line 144)\n     - Registers the edge in the graph: `g.Connect(edge)`\n\n**Example**: If a resource `aws_instance.web` references `aws_security_group.allow_http`, the ReferenceTransformer:\n1. Identifies the reference in the instance's configuration\n2. Finds the security group node in the graph\n3. Creates an edge: `aws_instance.web` → `aws_security_group.allow_http`\n4. This ensures the security group is created before the instance\n\n### ConfigTransformer - Resource Node Creation\n**File**: `internal/terraform/transform_config.go:17-30`\n\nThe `ConfigTransformer` adds nodes for all resources in the configuration:\n- Iterates over `config.Module.ManagedResources` and `config.Module.DataResources`\n- Creates concrete resource nodes using the provided `ConcreteResourceNodeFunc`\n- Only adds resources; variables, outputs, and providers are added separately\n- Handles import targets for `import` blocks\n\n### AttachStateTransformer - State Attachment\n**File**: `internal/terraform/transform_attach_state.go:35-63`\n\nThe `AttachStateTransformer` attaches prior run state to resource instance nodes:\n```go\nfunc (t *AttachStateTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error\n```\n\nFor each vertex implementing `GraphNodeAttachResourceState`:\n1. Provider Lifecycle\n**File**: `internal/terraform/graph_builder_plan.go:266`\n\nThe `CloseProviderTransformer` adds provider cleanup to the graph:\n- Creates edges to ensure providers are closed after all dependent resources complete\n- Prevents resource leaks and ensures proper plugin shutdown\n- Runs after all planning and refresh operations\n\n**Provider Lifecycle Summary**:\n1. **Instantiation**: `InitProvider()` creates plugin process\n2. **Validation**: `ValidateProvider()` validates configuration (during validation walk)\n3. **Configuration**: `ConfigureProvider()` configures the provider with credentials/settings\n4. **Usage**: Resources use the configured provider during planning/refresh\n5. **Cleanup**: `CloseProvider()` shuts down the plugin process\n\n## Q4: Diff Computation per Resource\n\n### Execution Entry Point - Synchronizing Remote State\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:580`\n\nThe `refresh()` method detects out-of-band changes to the remote resource:\n\n```go\nfunc (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext,\n  deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n  deferralAllowed bool) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, *providers.Deferred,\n  tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n```\n\n**Refresh Steps** (lines 580-741):\n1. **Pre-refresh Hook** (line 613): Calls hook to notify UI before refresh\n2. **Provider ReadResource RPC** (line 635):\n   ```go\n   resp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n     TypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n     PriorState: priorVal,\n     Private: state.Private,\n     ProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n     ClientCapabilities: {DeferralAllowed: deferralAllowed},\n   })\n   ```\n3. **State Update**: Updates state with the remote object's current state\n4. **Validation**: Ensures returned state conforms to schema\n5. **Returns**: New state reflecting remote reality, potential deferral indicator\n\n**Purpose**: The refresh detects:\n- Resources deleted outside of Terraform\n- Attribute changes made outside of Terraform (drift)\n- Resource still exists and is accessible\n\n#### Step 5: Plan Phase (lines 336-476)\n**Calls `n.plan()`** (unless `skipPlanChanges` is true):\n\n```go\nchange, instancePlanState, planDeferred, repeatData, planDiags :=\n  n.plan(ctx, nil, instanceRefreshState, n.ForceCreateBeforeDestroy,\n    n.forceReplace)\n```\n\n### Plan Method - Computing Desired Changes\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:744`\n\nThe `plan()` method computes what changes are needed to match configuration:\n\n```go\nfunc (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(ctx EvalContext,\n  plannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n  currentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n  createBeforeDestroy bool,\n  forceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n  *providers.Deferred, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n```\n\n**Plan Steps** (lines 744-1200+):\n\n1. **Configuration Evaluation** (lines 796-825):\n   - Evaluates the resource configuration block in context\n   - Handles `for_each`, `count` expressions\n   - Validates preconditions\n\n2. **Prior Value Preparation** (lines 834-894):\n   - Gets prior state value (from refresh)\n   - Handles tainted state (forces replace)\n   - Applies `ignore_changes` meta-argument\n\n3. **Proposed New Value** (line 896):\n   ```go\n   proposedNewVal := objchange.ProposedNew(schema,\n     unmarkedPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal)\n   ```\n   - Combines prior state with desired configuration\n   - Fills in provider-known computed values\n\n4. **Provider ValidateResourceConfig** (line 866):\n   - Calls provider to validate configuration is correct\n   - Catches configuration errors early\n\n5. **Provider PlanResourceChange RPC** (line 927):\n   ```go\n   resp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n     TypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n     Config: unmarkedConfigVal,\n     PriorState: unmarkedPriorVal,\n     ProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,\n     PriorPrivate: priorPrivate,\n     ProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n     ClientCapabilities: {DeferralAllowed: deferralAllowed},\n   })\n   ```\n   - Core RPC call to provider plugin\n   - Provider returns `PlannedState` and `RequiresReplace` paths\n   - Provider may also return deferred status\n\n6. **Action Determination** (line 1054):\n   ```go\n   action, actionReason := getAction(n.Addr, unmarkedPriorVal,\n     unmarkedPlannedNewVal, createBeforeDestroy, forceReplace, reqRep)\n   ```\n\n### getAction() - Determining Resource Action\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:2736`\n\nThe `getAction()` function determines what action to take based on plan analysis:\n\n```go\nfunc getAction(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, priorVal, plannedNewVal cty.Value,\n  createBeforeDestroy bool, forceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n  reqRep cty.PathSet) (action plans.Action, actionReason plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason)\n```\n\n**Action Determination Logic** (lines 2736-2774):\n\n1. **Create** (line 2762):\n   - When `priorVal.IsNull()` (no prior state)\n   - Resource is brand new\n\n2. **NoOp** (line 2764):\n   - When `eq && !matchedForceReplace`\n   - Prior and planned values are identical AND not force-replaced\n   - No changes needed\n\n3. **Replace** (lines 2765-2773):\n   - When `matchedForceReplace` (user specified `-replace=...`)\n   - OR `!reqRep.Empty()` (provider says certain paths require replacement)\n   - Determines replace strategy:\n     - `CreateThenDelete` if `createBeforeDestroy=true`\n     - `DeleteThenCreate` otherwise\n\n4. **Update** (implicit):\n   - If prior exists and planned is different\n   - And no paths require replacement\n   - Resource is modified in-place\n\n5. **Delete** (handled elsewhere):\n   - When resource is in state but not in configuration\n   - Handled by separate graph nodes (`OrphanResourceInstanceTransformer`)\n\n**Special Cases**:\n- **Tainted State** (lines 1143-1152): Tainted resources always force replace\n- **Replace Triggered By** (lines 393-395): Resources can be replaced by changes in other resources\n- **forceReplace Filtering** (line 1048): User `-replace=...` flags override provider logic\n\n### Change Recording (lines 404-431)\n- Writes the computed change to the plan: `n.writeChange(ctx, change, \"\")`\n- Writes the resulting state to working state: `n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instancePlanState, workingState)`\n- Checks `prevent_destroy` meta-argument\n- Evaluates postconditions\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Critical Files and Line References\n\n**Command and Backend**:\n- `internal/command/plan.go:22` - Transformer Sequence\n**File**: `internal/terraform/graph_builder_plan.go:121`\n\nThe `PlanGraphBuilder.Steps()` method returns a sequence of `GraphTransformer` stages that build the dependency graph:\n\n#### Stage 1: Node Creation (lines 135-202)\n1. **ConfigTransformer** (line 137): Creates resource nodes from configuration\n   - Adds all managed and data resources from the config tree\n   - Marks whether this is a destroy operation\n   - Handles import targets and configuration generation\n\n2. **Variable and Output Transformers** (lines 149-176):\n   - `RootVariableTransformer`: Adds root module variables with values\n   - `ModuleVariableTransformer`: Adds module-level variables\n   - `variableValidationTransformer`: Adds validation nodes\n   - `LocalTransformer`: Adds local value nodes\n   - `OutputTransformer`: Adds output value nodes\n\n3. **Orphan and Deposed Resource Handling** (lines 185-202):\n   - `OrphanResourceInstanceTransformer`: Adds nodes for resources in state but not config\n   - `StateTransformer`: Adds nodes for deposed resource instances (from failed replacements)\n   - `AttachStateTransformer` (line 205): **Attaches prior state to each resource instance node**\n\n#### Stage 2: Configuration and Provider Setup (lines 214-225)\n4. **AttachResourceConfigTransformer** (line 215): Attaches configuration blocks to resource nodes\n\n5. **Provider Transformation** (line 218): `transformProviders()` adds provider nodes\n   - Adds placeholder nodes for externally-configured providers\n   - Adds provider configuration nodes from the configuration\n\n6. **AttachSchemaTransformer** (line 225): **Must run before ReferenceTransformer**\n   - Attaches provider schemas to nodes\n   - Enables reference analysis based on schema information\n\n#### Stage 3: Module and Reference Processing (lines 227-239)\n7. **ModuleExpansionTransformer** (line 230): Creates expansion nodes for module calls\n\n8. **ExternalReferenceTransformer** (line 233): Preserves externally referenced nodes\n\n9. **ReferenceTransformer** (line 237): **Creates dependency edges from references**\n   - Analyzes all node references to find what each node depends on\n   - Connects edges from referencing nodes to their dependencies\n   - Implementation covered in detail below\n\n10. **AttachDependenciesTransformer** (line 239): Attaches explicit dependencies\n    - Processes depends_on arguments in resource configuration\n\n11. **attachDataResourceDependsOnTransformer** (line 243): Handles data resource depends_on\n\n#### Stage 4: Lifecycle and Cleanup (lines 245-274)\n12. **DestroyEdgeTransformer** (line 247): Creates edges for destroy operations\n13. **pruneUnusedNodesTransformer** (line 251): Removes unused nodes\n14. **TargetsTransformer** (line 256): Filters graph to only targeted resources (with dependencies)\n15. **ForcedCBDTransformer** (line 260): Forces create-before-destroy where needed\n16. **ephemeralResourceCloseTransformer** (line 263): Closes ephemeral resources\n17. **CloseProviderTransformer** (line 266): **Adds edges to properly close providers**\n18. **CloseRootModuleTransformer** (line 269): Closes the root module\n19. **TransitiveReductionTransformer** (line 273): Removes redundant edges\n\n### ReferenceTransformer - Dependency Edge Creation\n**File**: `internal/terraform/transform_reference.go:108-156`\n\nThe `ReferenceTransformer` analyzes configuration references to build dependency edges:\n\n```go\nfunc (t *ReferenceTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error\n```\n\n**Key Interface Requirements**:\n- **GraphNodeReferenceable**: Implemented by nodes that can be referenced (resources, modules, variables, outputs)\n  - `ReferenceableAddrs()`: Returns addresses through which this node can be referenced\n\n- **GraphNodeReferencer**: Implemented by nodes that reference other terraform objects\n  - `References()`: Returns a list of `addrs.Reference` objects being referenced\n\n**Algorithm** (lines 112-156):\n1. Builds a `ReferenceMap` from all graph vertices (line 115)\n2. For each vertex that implements `GraphNodeReferencer`:\n   - Calls `m.References(v)` to find parent dependencies (line 125)\n   - For each parent that is NOT a destroy node (to avoid cycles):\n     - Creates a `dag.BasicEdge` from the referencing node to the parent (line 144)\n     - Registers the edge in the graph: `g.Connect(edge)`\n\n**Example**: If a resource `aws_instance.web` references `aws_security_group.allow_http`, the ReferenceTransformer:\n1. Identifies the reference in the instance's configuration\n2. Finds the security group node in the graph\n3. Creates an edge: `aws_instance.web` → `aws_security_group.allow_http`\n4. This ensures the security group is created before the instance\n\n### ConfigTransformer - Resource Node Creation\n**File**: `internal/terraform/transform_config.go:17-30`\n\nThe `ConfigTransformer` adds nodes for all resources in the configuration:\n- Iterates over `config.Module.ManagedResources` and `config.Module.DataResources`\n- Creates concrete resource nodes using the provided `ConcreteResourceNodeFunc`\n- Only adds resources; variables, outputs, and providers are added separately\n- Handles import targets for `import` blocks\n\n### AttachStateTransformer - State Attachment\n**File**: `internal/terraform/transform_attach_state.go:35-63`\n\nThe `AttachStateTransformer` attaches prior run state to resource instance nodes:\n```go\nfunc (t *AttachStateTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error\n```\n\nFor each vertex implementing `GraphNodeAttachResourceState`:\n1. Gets the resource address from the vertex\n2. Looks up the corresponding resource in `t.State`\n3. Calls `AttachResourceState()` on the vertex with the prior state\n4. This state is used during planning to detect what changed\n\n## Q3: Provider Resolution and Configuration\n\n### Provider Initialization - EvalContext.InitProvider()\n**File**: `internal/terraform/eval_context.go:49-55`\n\nThe `EvalContext` interface defines provider initialization:\n```go\nInitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, configs *configs.Provider)\n  (providers.Interface, error)\n```\n\n**Implementation**: `internal/terraform/eval_context_builtin.go:138`\n\nThe `BuiltinEvalContext.InitProvider()` method:\n1. Returns the provider implementation\n\n**When Called**: During graph execution when a provider node is reached\n- Provider nodes implement `GraphNodeExecutable`\n- The graph walk reaches the provider node\n- `Execute()` calls `InitProvider()` to instantiate the plugin\n\n### Provider Configuration - NodeApplyableProvider.ConfigureProvider()\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_provider.go:99-110`\n\nAfter a provider is initialized, it must be configured:\n```go\nfunc (n *NodeApplyableProvider) ConfigureProvider(ctx EvalContext,\n  provider providers.Interface, verifyConfigIsKnown bool) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n```\n\nThis method:\n1. Provider Lifecycle\n**File**: `internal/terraform/graph_builder_plan.go:266`\n\nThe `CloseProviderTransformer` adds provider cleanup to the graph:\n- Creates edges to ensure providers are closed after all dependent resources complete\n- Prevents resource leaks and ensures proper plugin shutdown\n- Runs after all planning and refresh operations\n\n**Provider Lifecycle Summary**:\n1. **Instantiation**: `InitProvider()` creates plugin process\n2. **Validation**: `ValidateProvider()` validates configuration (during validation walk)\n3. **Configuration**: `ConfigureProvider()` configures the provider with credentials/settings\n4. **Usage**: Resources use the configured provider during planning/refresh\n5. **Cleanup**: `CloseProvider()` shuts down the plugin process\n\n## Q4: Diff Computation per Resource\n\n### Execution Entry Point - Determining Resource Action\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:2736`\n\nThe `getAction()` function determines what action to take based on plan analysis:\n\n```go\nfunc getAction(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, priorVal, plannedNewVal cty.Value,\n  createBeforeDestroy bool, forceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n  reqRep cty.PathSet) (action plans.Action, actionReason plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason)\n```\n\n**Action Determination Logic** (lines 2736-2774):\n\n1. **Create** (line 2762):\n   - When `priorVal.IsNull()` (no prior state)\n   - Resource is brand new\n\n2. **NoOp** (line 2764):\n   - When `eq && !matchedForceReplace`\n   - Prior and planned values are identical AND not force-replaced\n   - No changes needed\n\n3. **Replace** (lines 2765-2773):\n   - When `matchedForceReplace` (user specified `-replace=...`)\n   - OR `!reqRep.Empty()` (provider says certain paths require replacement)\n   - Determines replace strategy:\n     - `CreateThenDelete` if `createBeforeDestroy=true`\n     - `DeleteThenCreate` otherwise\n\n4. **Update** (implicit):\n   - If prior exists and planned is different\n   - And no paths require replacement\n   - Resource is modified in-place\n\n5. **Delete** (handled elsewhere):\n   - When resource is in state but not in configuration\n   - Handled by separate graph nodes (`OrphanResourceInstanceTransformer`)\n\n**Special Cases**:\n- **Tainted State** (lines 1143-1152): Tainted resources always force replace\n- **Replace Triggered By** (lines 393-395): Resources can be replaced by changes in other resources\n- **forceReplace Filtering** (line 1048): User `-replace=...` flags override provider logic\n\n### Change Recording (lines 404-431)\n- Writes the computed change to the plan: `n.writeChange(ctx, change, \"\")`\n- Writes the resulting state to working state: `n.writeResourceInstanceState(ctx, instancePlanState, workingState)`\n- Checks `prevent_destroy` meta-argument\n- Evaluates postconditions\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Critical Files and Line References\n\n**Command and Backend**:\n- `internal/command/plan.go:22` -
